scaling.  A base-law path may factor a fast analytic approximation:
\begin{equation*}
\begin{aligned}
  u(k,z)&=\log\!\left[\frac{P_{\rm truth}(k,z)}
                                  {P_{\rm base}(k,z)}\right],\\
  t(k,z)&=\frac{u(k,z)-\mu_u(k,z)}{s_u(k,z)}.
\end{aligned}
\end{equation*}
Inference reconstructs
\begin{equation*}
  \widehat P(k,z)
  =P_{\rm base}(k,z)
   \exp\!\left[\mu_u(k,z)+s_u(k,z)\widehat t(k,z)\right].
\end{equation*}
The base is evaluated at the same cosmology and coordinates as the target.
Its implementation identity, input names, domain, and version-independent
facts are part of the artifact contract.  A base from a different
implementation can have the same file shape and a different scientific
function.

For interpolation within an analytic base, both redshift and wavenumber grids
are finite, strictly increasing, and large enough for the declared spline
order.  \(k>0\) is required before \(\log k\).  Tail extrapolation parameters
are explicit, finite, and ordered.  The code retains the vendored
interpolation algorithm on valid inputs; validation makes its previously
implicit preconditions public.

\subsection{Bounded staging}

Production surfaces are wide.  Materializing every selected raw row in
float64 before thinning can exceed host memory even when the final float32
training matrix would fit.  Bounded staging therefore operates in chunks:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item read a bounded set of selected disk rows,
  \item cast to the payload dtype used by training,
  \item apply the base and logarithmic law,
  \item thin the \(k\) axis according to the declared stride,
  \item update stable streaming moments, and
  \item write the final compact rows to resident memory or an
        experiment-owned temporary memmap.
\end{enumerate}

Streaming variance uses a Chan/Welford merge of chunk counts, means, and
second central moments.  A sum/sum-of-squares formula suffers catastrophic
cancellation when values have a large offset and small spread.  The reference
is computed from the stored float32 payload because pre-cast float64 values
are not the data the geometry will encode.

Host-memory accounting includes both staged parameters and targets.  A
decision based only on target bytes can select a resident path that exceeds
the promised RAM fraction after the parameter copy is added.

\subsection{Temporary-file ownership}

A disk-backed staged target is a temporary resource owned by the experiment.
Train and validation slots are independent because validation may remain live
while successive training-size sweep points restage training rows.  Restaging
one slot unlinks the superseded file only after no live loader needs it.
Explicit release and failure cleanup remove remaining files.  Process-exit
cleanup is only a last defense; a long sweep cannot retain one multi-gigabyte
file per completed point.

\subsection{Hybrid inference}

EMUL2 is the repository's name for the hybrid inference configuration that
replaces several expensive provider products with coordinated emulator
artifacts.  In this EMUL2-shaped path, matter power, background history, and scalar
quantities can jointly replace expensive CAMB products inside a larger
likelihood.  The matter-power adapter validates requirements, rebuilds the
linear and boost artifacts, evaluates the current cosmology, reconstructs each
physical surface, and assembles \(P_{\rm nl}=P_{\rm lin}B\) when requested.

The derived quantity $\sigma_R$ is the root-mean-square linear density
contrast after smoothing with a spherical top-hat of comoving radius $R$:
\begin{align*}
 \sigma_R^2(z)&=\frac{1}{2\pi^2}
 \int_0^\infty dk\,k^2P_{\rm lin}(k,z)W^2(kR),\\
 W(x)&=3\,\frac{\sin x-x\cos x}{x^3}.
\end{align*}
The conventional $\sigma_8$ uses $R=8\,h^{-1}{\rm Mpc}$, where
$h=H_0/(100\,{\rm km\,s^{-1}\,Mpc^{-1}})$.  If the stored wavenumber is in
${\rm Mpc}^{-1}$, the numerical radius entering $kR$ is therefore
$8/h$ Mpc, not 8 Mpc.

\paragraph{Current gap.}
The adapter's derived \(\sigma_8\) helper currently combines \(k\) in
Mpc\(^{-1}\) with a radius of 8 Mpc, so it calculates \(\sigma(8\,\mathrm{Mpc})\)
rather than the conventional \(\sigma(8/h\,\mathrm{Mpc})\).  Matter-power
serving itself is unaffected.  The adapter also advertises products through
the wrong Cobaya support hook and narrows the shared \(A_s\)/\(A_{s,9}\)
amplitude rule.  Do not request the derived scalar or treat the stubbed
adapter identity as an EMUL2 dependency-resolution verdict.

\paragraph{Required closure.}
The ruled radius is the conventional $R=8\,h^{-1}{\rm Mpc}$ with no legacy
rename or dual serving.  Radius and wavenumber units are derived together, product registration
uses Cobaya's output boundary, and the amplitude requirement follows the
artifact's resolved parameterization.  A real Cobaya lifecycle gate requests
each product and reads it through the public provider.

The request boundary validates the full \(k\) and \(z\) sequences.  It also
rejects unsupported holes rather than zero-filling arbitrary missing
coordinates.  Every calculate call checks the external provider verdict
before reading payload getters, so a rejected point cannot inherit a previous
surface.

\subsection{Diagnostics and evidence}

Matter-power diagnostics plot residual surfaces and slices on the persisted
axes.  They avoid constructing a validation-rows by neighbors by full-width
cube at production scale; bounded diagnostics sample or stream the required
statistics.

The identity gate proves flatten/reshape, target laws, stable moments,
constant-column permission, base assembly, structured-head behavior, and
temporary-file lifecycle on controlled fixtures.  The smoke runs real CAMB,
two trainings, public \(P(k,z)\) getters, and family pages under the no-law
path.  Together they establish exact internal algebra and real-provider
connectivity without making the expensive provider its own reference.

\section{Diagnostics and plotting: compute a fact before drawing it}
\label{chap:diagnostics}

A \emph{diagnostic} calculates a statement about predictions.  A \emph{plot}
turns already calculated values into marks, lines, colors, and labels.  The
distinction is architectural: \code{emulator/diagnostics.py} owns estimators
and their validity conditions, while \code{emulator/plotting.py} owns visual
layout.  A plotting function must not silently invent a replacement statistic
when the diagnostic is undefined.

\subsection{The diagnostic record is a typed result}

For validation rows \(i=1,\ldots,N_{\rm val}\), the shared evaluation path first obtains
physical scores \(q_i=\Delta\chi_i^2\).  A coverage diagnostic may report
fractions such as
\begin{equation*}
 f_{<t}=\frac{1}{N_{\rm val}}
         \sum_{i=1}^{N_{\rm val}}{\bf 1}[q_i<t],
\end{equation*}
where \({\bf 1}[\cdot]\) is one when its condition is true and zero otherwise.
Here $N_{\rm val}$ is the number of held-out validation cosmologies, not the
training-set size or minibatch size.  The threshold \(t\), sample count
\(N_{\rm val}\), and side of the inequality are part
of the result.  A bare number such as \code{0.93} cannot reveal them.

A diagnostic dictionary therefore carries values together with names, units,
coordinate arrays, valid-row masks, and a status.  Status \code{available}
means the estimator's mathematical preconditions held.  Status
\code{unavailable} carries a reason such as ``no rows in this class'' or
``reference variance is zero.''  NaN is a floating-point value, not a complete
status record: it cannot distinguish a deliberate undefined result from
numerical corruption.

\subsection{Local-linear and hard-direction questions}

The local-linear diagnostic asks whether a small neighborhood can already
explain the validation target.  It selects nearby training rows, fits a local
linear approximation, and evaluates that approximation with the same physical
loss used for the emulator.  The neighborhood count, distance definition,
rank condition, and memory bound are estimator inputs; the neural model is not
the truth source for its own floor.

The hard-direction diagnostic relates poor scores to movement along named
parameter combinations.  Correlation and \(R^2\) require variation.  If a
feature is constant or a target class is empty, division by zero does not mean
``no relationship.''  It means the estimator is unavailable on that sample.
The result names that condition so the figure can annotate it instead of
plotting a fabricated zero.

\subsection{Family diagnostics retain their physical axes}

Scalar residuals are indexed by output name.  CMB residuals are indexed by
spectrum and multipole.  Background residuals are indexed by redshift and may
include distances derived through the real integration path.  Matter-power
residuals are two-dimensional surfaces over \((z,k)\).  Cosmic-shear residuals
retain correlation type, tomographic pair, and angle.  Reducing these objects
to one aggregate score is useful for model selection but insufficient for
finding a localized physical failure.

Fractional error, \((\widehat y-y)/y\), is undefined where \(y=0\).  The CMB
TE spectrum can cross zero, so a diagnostic uses an explicitly named mask or
an absolute-error alternative at the crossing.  A finite neural prediction
does not make division by a zero truth valid.

\subsection{The plotting layer is a consumer}

The page builder receives NumPy arrays on the CPU.  Model evaluation occurs
under \code{torch.no\_grad()} so the report does not retain a backward graph.
Tensor values are detached, moved to the CPU, and converted before Matplotlib
sees them.  This is an eager data transfer; the figure does not own a live GPU
tensor or a lazy loader.

Axis scale is chosen from the data domain.  A logarithmic ordinate requires
strictly positive finite values; a series containing zero remains linear or
uses a separately defined signed transformation.  Labels state estimator,
units, mask, and threshold.  A multipage writer saves completed figure objects
and closes them so long campaigns do not accumulate GUI and array state.

\paragraph{Current gap.}
Several diagnostic functions can currently publish NaN from empty classes,
zero-variance references, constant features, an unguarded standard deviation,
or a fractional residual at a truth zero.  Some smoke fixtures construct
finite diagnostic dictionaries by hand rather than executing those producer
functions.  Those tests prove plotting layout, not estimator totality.

\paragraph{Required closure.}
Every estimator validates finite inputs and its own denominator/rank/sample
preconditions, returns value plus status/reason, and is executed directly by
at least one board-listed diagnostic gate.  The save-before-diagnostics order
remains deliberate: a reporting failure must not destroy a successfully
trained artifact, but the report must never convert corruption into a green
``unavailable'' result.

\section{Saving, rebuilding, and predicting}
\label{chap:artifacts}

Training ends with a live Python object on one machine.  Inference needs a
self-contained record that can rebuild the same computation later.

\subsection{The two-file artifact}

The current format uses
\begin{table*}[t]
\centering
\begin{tabular}{p{0.21\textwidth}p{0.68\textwidth}}
\toprule
File & Contents \\
\midrule
\code{root.emul} & The model \code{state\_dict}: parameter and registered-buffer
names mapped to CPU tensors. \\
\code{root.h5} & Input/output geometry state, model recipe, resolved
configuration, histories, physical metadata, and optional NPCE/transfer base. \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\caption{The two files that currently form one saved emulator.  The
\code{.emul} file owns learned PyTorch tensors; the HDF5 \code{.h5} file owns
the constructor recipe and scientific coordinate facts needed to interpret
them.  They are written sequentially and are not yet digest-bound as one
transaction.}
\label{tab:artifact-files}
\end{table*}

A \code{state\_dict} is not a model object.  It contains numerical state but
not the Python constructor that gives those tensors meaning.  The Hierarchical
Data Format version 5 (HDF5) model recipe supplies the class name, dimensions,
and constructor options.

The two files answer different questions.  The weight file answers, ``what
numbers were learned?''  The HDF5 file answers, ``what calculation gives those
numbers meaning?''  A matching tensor width is not enough: the same-width
array could represent different multipoles, redshifts, output names, units, or
target laws.

One ordinary artifact has the following logical tree.  A slash denotes an
HDF5 group, which is a directory-like container.  A leaf such as
\code{center} is a dataset, an array stored inside the file.  A name after
\code{@} is an attribute, a small scalar fact attached to a group or to the
file itself.
\begin{verbatim}
root.emul
  tensor_name -> CPU tensor
root.h5
  @schema_version
  @git_commit
  model_recipe
    YAML constructor description
  config_resolved_yaml
    values consumed by the run
  param_geometry/
    @cls
    names, center, evecs, sqrt_ev
  dv_geometry/
    @cls
    center, coordinates
    covariance factors
  history/
    train_losses, val_medians
    val_means, val_fracs
\end{verbatim}
Here, \code{tensor\_name} stands for each registered parameter or buffer name,
and \code{@cls} names the Python class whose \code{from\_state} constructor
interprets that group.  The slash syntax above is explanatory; HDF5 does not
store a Unix directory.
The recursive writer walks a nested Python dictionary.  A nested dictionary
becomes a group, a numerical array becomes a dataset, and selected scalar
facts become attributes.  The recursive reader performs the inverse walk and
moves reconstructed tensors to the requested device.

Optional model compositions add owners rather than changing the meaning of
the ordinary fields:
\begin{table*}[t]
\centering
\begin{tabular}{p{0.15\textwidth}p{0.31\textwidth}p{0.44\textwidth}}
\toprule
Artifact kind & Main \code{.emul} tensors & Additional HDF5 owner \\
\midrule
Ordinary & The complete predictor network & No optional model group. \\
NPCE & The neural residual or ratio refiner & \code{pce/} stores the frozen
polynomial basis, coefficients, output modes, fitted box, and composition
form. \\
Transfer & The correction network & \code{transfer\_base/} embeds the frozen
base recipe, base tensors, both base geometries, and the declared sum/gain
composition facts. \\
Refined transfer & The correction network & The original base state remains
as provenance; \code{drifted\_state/} stores the jointly updated base.  A
native-boolean marker and group presence must agree before that state is
selected. \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\caption{Tensor ownership in the four artifact compositions.  Rebuilding
does not infer an optional component from shape.  Its named group and required
facts must be present.}
\end{table*}

\paragraph{Current gap.}
The two current files are written independently.  The HDF5 record does not
carry a digest of the weight file, and publication is not a two-file
transaction.  Replacing one file, mixing roots, or interrupting an overwrite
can therefore create a pair that exists but was never published together.

\paragraph{Required closure.}
The pair is staged under temporary names, validated, and published as one
logical unit.  Each side binds the same artifact identity and the HDF5 record
binds the exact weight payload and implementation identity.  Pre-existing
trusted roots are refused rather than silently overwritten.  Strict tensor
loading remains necessary, but matching tensor names and shapes is not a
substitute for pair identity.

\subsection{Moving tensors into storage}

For a model tensor $w$,
\code{w.detach()} returns a tensor disconnected from gradient history, but it
normally shares the same numerical storage with $w$.  Detachment changes what
autograd records; it is not a copy operation.  Calling \code{w.cpu()} copies
accelerator storage to host memory when necessary, but a tensor already on the
CPU may be returned without a copy.  Calling \code{w.numpy()} on a compatible
CPU tensor presents that storage as a NumPy array and normally shares memory
with it.  An in-place write through either object can then change the other.
Use an explicit \code{clone()} or NumPy \code{copy()} when the receiving caller
must own independent mutable storage.

Serialization is a later boundary.  Writing a tensor or NumPy array to a
PyTorch or HDF5 file copies its current bytes into the file; the file does not
retain a live pointer to process memory.  Reading it later constructs new
process-owned storage.  Saving CPU tensors therefore lets a machine without
the training GPU open the artifact, but moving to CPU alone is not proof that
an in-process returned array is independent.

HDF5 uses groups, datasets, and attributes.  A group is a directory-like
container.  A dataset is an array payload.  An attribute is scalar metadata
attached to a group or file.  Nested geometry dictionaries become nested
groups through a recursive writer.

\subsection{Rebuilding the geometry class}

Each geometry group stores a class string such as
\code{emulator.geometries.parameter.ParamGeometry}.  Rebuilding performs four
steps:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item split the string into module path and class name,
  \item import the module,
  \item retrieve the class object, and
  \item call that class's \code{from\_state} constructor.
\end{enumerate}
Using the persisted class prevents a factored or logarithmic geometry from
silently rebuilding as its simpler base class.

\subsection{Rebuilding the model}

The model recipe stores factory choices as names because a Python callable
cannot be represented directly in YAML.  Rebuilding translates those names
back into activation and normalization factories, constructs the eager model,
and loads the weights with \code{strict=True}.  Strict loading rejects both
missing and unexpected keys.

A compiled model wraps the eager module and may prefix state keys with
\code{\_orig\_mod.}.  Saving removes that wrapper prefix.  Rebuilding loads the
plain state first and compiles afterward when requested and supported.

\subsection{Prediction}

\code{EmulatorPredictor.predict} performs the five transitions in
Table~\ref{tab:prediction-trace}.  The table separates the source of each fact
from the object produced by the transition.

\begin{table*}[t]
\centering
\begin{tabular}{p{0.08\textwidth}p{0.24\textwidth}p{0.27\textwidth}p{0.30\textwidth}}
\toprule
Step & Input & Operation and owner & Output \\
\midrule
1 & Parameter dictionary & Order values by the parameter names stored in the
artifact, refusing missing or unexpected names & Raw row
$\Theta\in\mathbb{R}^{1\times P}$. \\
2 & Raw parameter row & Parameter geometry centers, rotates, and scales &
Encoded row $X\in\mathbb{R}^{1\times P_{\rm enc}}$ on the model device. \\
3 & Encoded row & Eager or compiled model in evaluation mode under
\code{no\_grad} & Network output $\widehat T$ in encoded coordinates. \\
4 & Encoded network output plus encoded input row & The branch-specific
decoder composes any PCE base, amplitude law, intrinsic-alignment templates,
or transfer correction and invokes the saved output geometry & A decoded kept
row.  It is physical for scalar, background, CMB, and ordinary data-vector
families; grid2d remains in its declared law space. \\
5 & Decoded kept row & Family packaging restores a data-vector layout or
attaches saved names and axes.  The matter-power consumer performs the
separately owned analytic-base multiplication & A scalar dictionary, a
physical CMB/background/data-vector result, or a grid2d law-space surface on
the stored $(z,k)$ axes. \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\caption{One prediction from a named cosmology.  The caller supplies parameter
values; the artifact supplies their order and every output-side scientific
fact.}
\label{tab:prediction-trace}
\end{table*}

Evaluation mode disables training-only behavior.  \code{torch.no\_grad()}
avoids constructing a backward graph, reducing memory and latency.  The
artifact's parameter names, axes, units, and laws determine the result; the
caller does not redeclare them.

\paragraph{Current returned-array ownership gap.}
For a CPU background prediction, the returned NumPy \code{z} array can share
storage with the geometry's cached PyTorch axis.  A caller that changes
\code{result["z"]} in place can therefore change the predictor's saved axis,
and the next prediction can report the mutated coordinates.  The corresponding
MPS axis conversion currently copies, so the same caller mutation has
device-dependent consequences.  Returning a view of a derived cached tensor
would create the same problem even when the tensor is not a named geometry
attribute.

\paragraph{Required closure.}
Public prediction and diagnostic dictionaries own their returned numerical
arrays.  Every axis and value array is a defensive copy after detaching and
moving to the CPU.  A gate mutates each returned array in place, calls the same
predictor again, and proves that geometry state and the second result are
unchanged on CPU, MPS, and CUDA where supported.  The implementation census
starts with \code{.numpy()} calls but also follows helper functions that return
views of cached tensors.

\subsection{Rebuild ledger: which file answers each question?}

Loading an artifact is not equivalent to unpickling one object.  Rebuilding
constructs new Python objects and then fills them with validated stored facts.
The sequence is:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item open the HDF5 record and validate its schema;
  \item rebuild input and output geometries from their named classes and
        stored arrays;
  \item resolve the model, activation, normalization, and loss classes from
        the stored recipe;
  \item instantiate an eager model with the persisted dimensions;
  \item read the tensor mapping from \code{root.emul} onto the CPU;
  \item load every expected key with \code{strict=True};
  \item move the complete predictor to the requested device; and
  \item compile only after eager reconstruction when compilation is requested
        and supported.
\end{enumerate}

Each implemented step has a different refusal.  An unknown geometry class
fails before a network is built.  A missing tensor key fails strict loading.
A CMB axis that has the right width and the wrong multipoles fails coordinate
validation.  These errors are not redundant: each names the first current
boundary that can identify a particular inconsistency.

Pair identity is not yet one of those current boundaries.  Under the required
closure above, a weight file with a different digest would fail before its
apparently compatible tensors were loaded.  Today, mixing two artifacts with
the same expected tensor names and shapes can pass strict loading because the
HDF5 file does not bind the exact \code{.emul} bytes.  This is why the
two-file gap remains a scientific-integrity issue rather than a documentation
detail.

The reconstructed model is a new owner of its tensors.  Moving it to CUDA or
MPS copies CPU state to the accelerator; the HDF5 datasets and the NumPy
objects used during loading do not become live device parameters.  The
predictor retains the geometry and model objects it needs.  Closing the HDF5
file therefore does not invalidate a correctly rebuilt predictor.

\section{Cobaya adapters: presenting the emulator as a theory component}
\label{chap:adapters}

Cobaya asks a theory component for named quantities at a sampled cosmology.
The adapters in \code{cobaya\_theory/} translate that lifecycle into an
\code{EmulatorPredictor} call.

\subsection{Lifecycle methods}

\begin{table*}[t]
\centering
\begin{tabular}{p{0.22\textwidth}p{0.66\textwidth}}
\toprule
Method & Responsibility \\
\midrule
\code{initialize} & Validate options, choose device, load artifacts, and cache
immutable metadata. \\
\code{get\_requirements} & Declare sampled or provider-supplied inputs needed
by the prediction. \\
\code{must\_provide} & Validate the requested output coordinates and record
what the likelihood asks for. \\
\code{calculate} & Build the parameter mapping, call the predictor, validate
the returned payload, and place it in the current state. \\
Getter methods & Return named arrays from the accepted current state. \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\caption{Cobaya theory-component lifecycle in call order.  Initialization
constructs immutable machinery; requirements describe needed inputs;
\code{must\_provide} records the requested output; each \code{calculate}
replaces per-cosmology state; getters expose only that accepted current state.}
\label{tab:cobaya-lifecycle}
\end{table*}

The adapter is a boundary between untyped configuration values and numerical
code.  Boolean, integer, float, path, and list options require explicit value
validation; Python truthiness and numeric coercion must not reinterpret quoted
strings or NaN.

\paragraph{Current gap.}
The five adapters do not yet share a total value-schema boundary.  Several
options are interpreted with \code{bool(value)}, relative roots can inherit an
empty environment default, and some requested coordinates are coerced before
validation.  The scalar adapter also does not yet exercise its real
\code{state["derived"]} publication path in the existing identity double.

\paragraph{Required closure.}
One shared validator checks actual booleans, finite numeric controls, explicit
path roots, exact requested coordinates, and family-compatible artifact
assembly before any artifact is loaded or provider result is published.  A
gate calls the public Cobaya lifecycle, not merely the predictor helper, and
reads the value back through the same getter a likelihood uses.

\subsection{Requested coordinates are part of the contract}

An output width is not an axis.  Two multipole arrays can have equal length
and different values.  Two redshift grids can have equal length and different
sampling.  \code{must\_provide} validates the complete requested coordinate
sequence against the persisted artifact sequence before any calculation can
return a value.

\paragraph{Current gap.}
That exact-sequence sentence is the required contract, not uniform current
behavior.  The CMB adapter presently checks a maximum multipole and can
scatter a request containing interior holes into a zero-filled array.  CMB
training dumps also lack an authoritative multipole sidecar, so equal width
can silently relabel shifted columns.  Other family adapters have analogous
range-versus-identity gaps.

\paragraph{Required closure.}
The generator publishes the exact coordinate sequence; staging verifies it;
the artifact persists the verified sequence; and \code{must\_provide}
requires exact ordered coordinates or a separately defined subset policy.
Missing interior coordinates never become physical zeros.

When several artifacts contribute blocks to one output vector, the adapter
must prove that the layouts are compatible and the destination blocks do not
overlap.  Blind concatenation is not a layout proof.

\subsection{State ownership}

One \code{calculate} call corresponds to one sampled cosmology.  A rejected
external calculation must not expose arrays cached by an earlier cosmology.
The acceptance verdict is checked before any provider getter is called, and
the current state is replaced only by payloads produced for the current point.

\paragraph{Current gap.}
The preceding ordering is not yet uniform across generators and adapters.
Several paths infer rejection by scanning text or read a provider payload
before establishing the current calculation's finite verdict; a stale cached
array can therefore look successful.  A fake that always returns a fresh
payload does not exercise this failure mode.

\paragraph{Required closure.}
One verdict-first helper handles the real provider return object.  Rejection
performs zero getters and publishes no state.  Acceptance is recorded before
the first getter, and a two-call stale-cache fixture tags generations so any
payload inherited from the previous cosmology fails visibly.

\subsection{Worked lifecycle: one CMB likelihood request}

Assume the configuration loads one temperature-spectrum artifact whose stored
axis is $\ell=2,\ldots,2500$.  Initialization opens the two artifact files,
rebuilds the predictor, records that it provides \code{tt}, and takes the
union of the predictor's saved parameter names.  That union becomes the
dictionary returned by \code{get\_requirements}.  No sampled cosmology has
been evaluated yet.

A likelihood can then declare a request equivalent to
\begin{verbatim}
Cl:
  tt: 2000
\end{verbatim}
Cobaya forwards this declaration to \code{must\_provide}.  The method checks
that a loaded artifact provides \code{tt} and that the requested maximum does
not exceed 2500.  This is request negotiation: it happens when Cobaya assembles
the component graph, before the first Markov-chain point.  A request for
\code{ee}, or for \code{tt} through 3000, is refused here rather than becoming
a truncated prediction.

For one accepted sampled point, Cobaya calls \code{calculate} with a mutable
\code{state} dictionary and named parameter values.  The adapter passes those
values to the predictor.  It allocates a \code{float64} array covering
$0,\ldots,2500$, writes predicted values at the artifact's multipoles, and
stores the completed mapping under \code{state["Cl"]}.  The zeros below
$\ell=2$ are conventional storage positions, not neural-network predictions.

Finally, the likelihood calls \code{get\_Cl}.  The getter reads
\code{self.current\_state["Cl"]}, which Cobaya associates with the current
sample.  It refuses an unrequested unit or plotting-factor conversion rather
than silently changing the training convention.  The getter does not call the
network again.

\begin{table*}[t]
\centering
\begin{tabular}{p{0.18\textwidth}p{0.21\textwidth}p{0.29\textwidth}p{0.21\textwidth}}
\toprule
Lifecycle time & Method & State it may change & Failure meaning \\
\midrule
Component construction & \code{initialize} & Immutable predictors, axes,
requirements & Artifact or option cannot define a component. \\
Graph negotiation & \code{must\_provide} & Recorded output request & A
downstream likelihood asks for an unsupported product or coordinate. \\
One sampled point & \code{calculate} & The supplied current-point state & The
named cosmology cannot produce a valid current payload. \\
Likelihood read & \code{get\_Cl} or family getter & No numerical state; reads
the current payload & The consumer asks for an unsupported serving convention. \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\caption{Cobaya lifecycle time is part of ownership.  Validation at one row
cannot substitute for validation at component construction or request
negotiation.}
\end{table*}

The present CMB adapter negotiates by spectrum name and maximum multipole.  It
does not yet prove that an arbitrary interior coordinate sequence exactly
matches the artifact.  The earlier coordinate-contract subsection records
that open boundary.  The worked example explains current execution without
mistaking the current maximum-only check for the stronger queued rule.

\section{Gates: executable evidence that the pipeline still means what it says}
\label{chap:gates}

A gate is a test whose failure blocks acceptance of a program unit.  The board
is the ordered list of gates.  Each entry names its dependencies, required
software or hardware, owning documentation, and executable check.

\subsection{Identity checks and smoke checks}

An identity check isolates mathematics and serialization with small synthetic
inputs.  A smoke check runs a short real external pipeline, such as CAMB or
CosmoLike, and proves that the components connect on the production path.
Neither substitutes for the other.

An identity check should contain four named pieces:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item the production function or public boundary under test,
  \item a small fixture, meaning a constructed input with known properties,
  \item an independently calculated expected answer, and
  \item a deliberately broken form that the check must reject.
\end{enumerate}

The deliberately broken form establishes catch power: the assertion is not
merely true of both correct and incorrect implementations.

\subsection{Test doubles}

A test double replaces an expensive or unavailable collaborator.  A stub
returns predetermined values.  A fake implements a small working substitute.
A monkeypatch temporarily replaces the referenced function or class during a
test.  Every double must state which behavior it reproduces and which external
behavior it cannot prove.

An independently known answer cannot be computed by the same helper that
produces the value under test.  Shared code would reproduce the same defect on
both sides of the comparison.

\subsection{Exit status and the board}

Each check records failures and exits nonzero when any assertion fails.  The
board judges the subprocess exit status and required output.  Printing a skip
message while returning zero is not a skip; without a distinct board status it
is a pass.

Board resume records are scientifically valid only for the executable surface
that produced them.  The present runner records status, a digest of the gate
body and directly named check scripts, an input/configuration digest, and a
digest of the raw log.  A changed gate, directly named check script, board
configuration, YAML, or raw-log payload therefore invalidates the stored PASS
automatically.

Before a run, preflight also requires a clean executable surface.  It watches
\code{emulator/}, \code{gates/}, \code{compute\_data\_vectors/},
\code{cobaya\_theory/}, \code{syren/}, and the top-level Python drivers.  A
dirty generator or adapter is therefore refused just like a dirty training
module.  This check establishes that the evidence can be tied to a committed
tree; it does not decide which committed files belong to one particular gate.

The per-gate code digest now has two regimes.  A gate that declares an
executable manifest digests its resolved membership: the declared root
modules, every repo-local file they import transitively, the check scripts
its body names, and the shared runner, member by member.  A gate that
declares nothing keeps the narrower legacy digest of its body and directly
named check scripts.  Every live gate is currently in the second regime, so
a committed production-only change can still leave its stored digest
unchanged.  Force-rerun remains the manual safeguard for those gates until
per-gate population assigns exact owners.

Raw-log integrity no longer has that asymmetry.  The resume decision and the
display use the same predicate.  A PASS whose cited log is absent, lacks a
stored digest, or has edited bytes becomes \code{stale-log}; it neither skips
the selected gate nor satisfies a downstream dependency.  The board self-test
drives the real resume function through deletion, truncation, edit, and
missing-digest cases and includes a tamper arm that flips a current PASS to
\code{stale-log}.

Hardware-specific PyTorch evidence belongs in a board-listed gate.  CPU-only
checks can prove pure validation and algebra.  CUDA compilation, GPU dtype,
and accelerator-specific behavior require execution on the corresponding
workstation.

\section{One complete row through the program}
\label{chap:trace}

The entire pipeline can now be read as one sequence.  Consider generated row
$i$, containing cosmology $\btheta_i$ and target $\bd_i$.

\begin{enumerate}
  \item The path resolver converts YAML file names to absolute paths.
  \item The experiment validates the selected family and records parameter
        names from the covariance header.
  \item Staging opens the data-vector dump lazily, loads the parameter table,
        verifies row counts, applies physical cuts, and selects row $i$ as
        part of a seeded subset.
  \item The source dictionary records how to address row $i$ in resident or
        file-backed storage.
  \item The parameter geometry transforms $\btheta_i$ into whitened input
        $x_i$.
  \item The output geometry and any target law transform $\bd_i$ into target
        $t_i$.
  \item A loader returns $x_i$ and $t_i$ on the model device as
        \code{float32} tensors.
  \item The model predicts $\widehat t_i$.
  \item The loss reconstructs the final physical prediction, forms the
        residual, and computes $\Delta\chi_i^2$.
  \item Backward differentiation computes parameter gradients.  The finite
        checks, optional clipping, optimizer, anchor, and moving average act in
        their defined order.
  \item Validation scores every held-out row and selects a best epoch whose
        weights and metrics refer to the same state.
  \item Saving writes model tensors plus the resolved recipe and geometries.
  \item Rebuilding reconstructs the eager model, loads weights strictly, and
        restores physical metadata from the artifact.
  \item The predictor accepts a named cosmology, repeats the saved encode,
        model, and branch-specific decode chain.  Most families return physical
        units; grid2d returns the declared law-space surface and its consumer
        applies the persisted analytic base to obtain physical $P(k,z)$.
  \item A Cobaya adapter exposes that result under the requested theory-product
        name and coordinate grid.
  \item Identity and smoke gates prove the mathematical, serialization, and
        external-pipeline boundaries independently.
\end{enumerate}

The network is only one step in this chain.  Most silent scientific failures
occur at the boundaries: a mismatched row, an unnamed axis, a scale that
underflows in storage, a target law applied on only one side, a stale external
provider result, or a saved recipe that does not describe the weights.  The
architecture matters, but the program is trustworthy only when every boundary
states and checks what its numbers mean.

\subsection{Object ledger for the same row}

The symbol $i$ does not have one universal coordinate meaning throughout the
program.  Before staging, it can denote an original dump row.  After a sorted
unique RAM gather, the same physical cosmology has a local compact-array
coordinate.  During an epoch it has a position in a new seeded permutation.
The row payload is unchanged only if the coordinate maps are applied
correctly.

\begin{table*}[t]
\centering
\begin{tabular}{p{0.17\textwidth}p{0.22\textwidth}p{0.26\textwidth}p{0.24\textwidth}}
\toprule
Boundary & Object before & Object after & Equality that should hold \\
\midrule
Row staging & Original dump row coordinate & Resident-local or disk-global
coordinate plus \code{dump\_rows} & Parameter row and every sibling target
come from the same original row. \\
Parameter geometry & $\theta_i$ in physical units & $x_i$ in dimensionless
network coordinates & \code{decode(encode(theta\_i))} returns $\theta_i$. \\
Output geometry & $d_i$ on a named physical axis & $t_i$ in target coordinates
& Decode returns $d_i$ on the identical axis. \\
Model and loss & $(x_i,t_i)$ & $(\widehat t_i,\Delta\chi_i^2)$ & Whitened and
direct physical contractions agree. \\
Artifact & Live classes and tensors & Weight payload plus HDF5 recipe & Rebuilt
eager prediction matches the live eager prediction. \\
Adapter & Named cosmology and requested axis & Current Cobaya theory product &
Getter readback equals the predictor output in the declared serving convention. \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\caption{Six identities for one row.  A shape check alone proves none of
them.}
\end{table*}

Take a cosmic-shear row as a concrete example.  The original parameter table
might store 17 cosmological and nuisance parameters, while a physical cut
retains 12 as the model input and a likelihood mask retains 780 of a larger
data vector.  Staging first proves that the parameter row and target row share
one original coordinate.  The parameter geometry returns a $(1,12)$ tensor.
The output geometry returns a $(1,780)$ target.  The model preserves the batch
dimension and predicts another $(1,780)$ tensor.  The output geometry and
loss use the persisted mask and covariance to give one scalar
$\Delta\chi_i^2$.

Neither $(1,12)$ nor $(1,780)$ states which cosmology, mask, or axis was used.
The row-coordinate maps, parameter names, destination indices, and covariance
owner provide that meaning.  Saving those facts is therefore part of saving
the model, even though none is a learned weight.

\subsection{Rebuilding every vector figure}

Every numbered scientific figure in this manuscript is generated by
\code{texnotes/make\_figures.py}.  The script has one named function per
figure and writes vector PDF files under \code{texnotes/figures/}.  Vector
output stores lines, text, and curves as drawing instructions, so labels
remain sharp when the paper is enlarged.  No screenshot is the source of a
manuscript figure.

From the repository root, rebuild the complete set with
\begin{verbatim}
python3 texnotes/make_figures.py
\end{verbatim}
and then rebuild the paper.  The script prints one \code{wrote} line for each
expected figure.  It does not import the emulator package or require PyTorch;
the diagrams explain fixed program structure, and the activation curves use
their formulas directly.  Keeping figure generation independent of training
prevents an unavailable GPU from blocking documentation builds.

The compiled \code{texnotes/emulator\_code\_guide.pdf} remains tracked so a
reader can open the guide without installing LaTeX.  That convenience creates
a freshness obligation: after any change to this source or a numbered figure,
the PDF must be rebuilt and visually inspected before the change lands.  The
present landing follows that rule.  A future documentation lane should compare
the tracked PDF with a clean rebuild and fail on different bytes; until that
check exists, the rebuild is a required manual acceptance step rather than an
inferred property of the \code{.tex} timestamp.

The residual-block figure is tied to the executed operation order documented
in Sec.~\ref{chap:models}: every internal dense layer maps $W$ to $W$, the
skip is added after the final internal dense layer, and the final normalization
and activation follow the addition.  The activation figure places each legend
outside its data rectangle so no label hides a curve.  Regenerating the
figures after a structural code change is necessary but not sufficient; the
caption and implementation must still be compared during review.

\appendix
\section{The gate board, one executable claim at a time}
\label{app:gates}

This appendix explains all forty gates currently registered in
\code{gates/board.py}, in exact board order.  A first-time contributor needs
to know not only what a gate is called, but what production path it executes,
what its fixture means, which value determines the verdict, and which
plausible defect it can catch.

\subsection{How to read each gate description}

Every description below answers five questions: the claim made credible by a
pass; the production path executed; the controlled fixture; the numeric,
artifact, or loud-error verdict; and the deliberately wrong behavior that
establishes catch power.

\begin{figure*}[t]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=0.94\textwidth]
  {texnotes/figures/fig10_board_flow.pdf}
\caption{The board's evidence flow.  Preflight and selection determine what
is eligible to run; the gate body produces evidence; the board converts all
required claims into one explicit verdict.}
\label{fig:board-flow}
\end{figure*}

An identity gate usually uses a small analytic fixture and asks whether a
transformation, save/rebuild cycle, or composition preserves a known value.
A smoke gate runs a short production-shaped calculation and asks whether
independently implemented components connect.  A golden run compares selected
output from the current tree with a pinned earlier tree.  Golden equality is
useful for an advertised no-op mode, but it cannot validate behavior that did
not exist in the pinned tree.

\subsection{Gate vocabulary in plain language}

\begin{description}
  \item[Fixture.] A deliberately small input prepared for a check.  Its
  coordinates and expected answer are known before the production function
  runs.

  \item[Control.] A nearby case known to be valid.  A positive control must
  pass; a negative control must be refused.  Controls prevent a gate from
  becoming red merely because its harness is broken.

  \item[Mutation arm.] A deliberately wrong implementation or input form
  inserted only in the test.  It represents a plausible defect, such as a
  transposed axis or an inflated tolerance.

  \item[Catch power.] Evidence that the gate turns red for the mutation
  arm.  Agreement on the correct fixture without a discriminating wrong arm
  can be a coincidence.

  \item[Parity.] Equality between two paths that are required to implement
  the same function, for example eager and compiled evaluation.  Parity alone
  does not establish that either path is scientifically correct, so it is
  paired with an independent answer.

  \item[Census.] A mechanical enumeration of every member of a source-code
  class, such as every model constructor or every assertion site.  A census
  prevents a repair from covering only the first instance found.

  \item[Banner.] Human-readable run text reporting a resolved setting.  A
  banner is useful provenance, but construction or numerical behavior must
  prove that the reported setting was actually used.

  \item[Sidecar.] A small companion file that gives meaning to a larger
  numerical dump, for example column names or an axis array.  Row-for-row and
  artifact-identity rules determine which sidecar belongs to which payload.

  \item[Golden run.] Output pinned from an earlier executable tree for a
  behavior promised to remain unchanged.  It is a regression reference, not
  an independent derivation of new mathematics.

  \item[Collapse bar.] A threshold that a model which learned no useful
  dependence cannot beat.  It turns a short smoke from ``the program ran''
  into a minimal liveness claim.

  \item[Provenance.] Facts identifying how a result was produced: source
  digest, resolved configuration, coordinates, dtype, device, and artifact
  identity.  Provenance permits a reviewer to reconstruct the claim's scope.
\end{description}

\subsection{The board runner as a small execution system}

\code{gates/run\_board.py} is the command-line runner.
\code{gates/board.py} is the declarative registry.  Keeping them separate
means the list of scientific claims does not reimplement subprocess, path, or
resume handling.  A board entry supplies an identifier, title, tier, home
documentation, capability requirements, dependencies, and a Python function
that expresses the gate body through a constrained context object.

The context object is the gate's interface to the outside world.  It can
resolve a configured path, launch a check script, launch a driver, record a
message, and assert an expected condition.  The gate body does not call
\code{subprocess} directly.  This restriction gives the runner one place to
capture command lines, standard output, standard error, return status, and
elapsed time.

Standard output is the normal text stream a process prints.  Standard error is
a separate stream intended for diagnostics.  Exit status zero conventionally
means success and nonzero means failure.  The runner records all three.
Checking only for a phrase is insufficient if the process later exits
nonzero; checking only exit zero is insufficient if the expected scientific
assertion never ran.

\subsection{A declared claim is not yet an executed claim}

The registry is beginning to represent an acceptance leg with two strings: a
plain identifier and an anchor in its home note.  The identifier names the
specific observation, such as \code{stage-ram.exact-fit-boundary}.  The anchor
points to the paragraph that defines what result is acceptable.  Registry
validation can prove that the anchor exists and that no two legs share an
identifier.

Those checks establish declaration, not execution.  Suppose a gate declares
three legs but a conditional return skips the third.  The remaining two can
pass and the subprocess can exit zero unless the runner compares the declared
and executed sets.  The complete mechanism therefore needs one terminal
record per declared leg:
\begin{equation*}
 D=E,
\end{equation*}
where \(D\) is the set of declared identifiers and \(E\) is the set of
identifiers with an executed terminal result: \code{PASS}, \code{FAIL}, or
\code{UNAVAILABLE}.
\code{UNAVAILABLE} is non-green.  It states that a required hardware or
software lane did not run; it does not shrink the denominator and turn the
remaining legs into a complete pass.  A crash before a check script emits its
record is likewise a missing leg and makes the gate red.

A three-leg example makes the set equality concrete.  Suppose the registry
declares
\begin{equation*}
 D=\{\code{roundtrip},\code{wrong-axis},\code{real-provider}\}.
\end{equation*}
The check executes the first two legs and then returns before contacting the
provider.  Its executed set is
\begin{equation*}
 E=\{\code{roundtrip},\code{wrong-axis}\}.
\end{equation*}
Both emitted results can say \code{PASS}, but $D\ne E$: the missing
\code{real-provider} leg makes the gate red.  Conversely, an emitted id that
does not occur in $D$ is also an error because it cannot be matched to a
reviewed claim.  \code{ctx.expect(label, condition)} is the in-process helper
used by migrated gate bodies: \code{label} names the leg and \code{condition}
is the boolean verdict.  A false condition records failure; it is not merely
an informational print.

\paragraph{Current gap.}
Only a small migrated subset of gates carries structured headline evidence.
The runner verifies anchor existence and global identifier uniqueness, but it
does not yet reconcile each declared leg with a result emitted by
\code{ctx.expect} or by an external check script.

\paragraph{Required closure.}
Every gate uses a human-readable \code{<gate-id>.<leg-name>} identifier, every
anchor belongs to the gate's declared home note, and every run emits exactly
one terminal result per leg.  Unknown, duplicate, and missing executed ids all
fail before the gate can be recorded as passed.

\subsection{Preflight protects expensive evidence}

Preflight runs before GPU time.  It checks the expected Git tip, watched-tree
cleanliness, required imports, and configured data paths.  A workstation log
is evidence about one executable surface.  If the worktree contains
unrecorded modifications, the log cannot be reproduced from the named commit.

Import checks are capability checks, not substitutes for gate execution.
Importing PyTorch proves that the module loads; it does not prove CUDA
kernels, compilation, or mixed precision.  Opening a Cocoa data directory
proves deployment availability, not that a family adapter requests the right
physical quantity.

\paragraph{Current watched-tree status.}
The watched directory list now includes \code{emulator/}, \code{gates/},
\code{compute\_data\_vectors/}, \code{cobaya\_theory/}, \code{syren/}, and the
root drivers.  The porcelain-status parser now preserves Git's leading
two-column status field before examining individual lines.  It excludes
exactly \code{gates/board\_config.json}; an edit to neighboring
\code{gates/board.py} remains dirty.  Self-test fixtures exercise the case in
which the permitted config file is the first status line, because a whole-
output \code{strip()} previously shifted that line alone.  This clean-tree
surface is shared by the report and the executed preflight decision.

\paragraph{Current execution-root gap.}
The runner resolves and prints the project root selected by board
configuration, but a launched child can still inherit an older shell
\code{ROOTDIR}.  A check run whose report names root B can therefore open data
below root A.  The mismatch is especially easy to miss when a check resolves a
path before the runner's intended environment-injection point: subsequent
logging cannot change the already chosen file.

\paragraph{Required execution-root closure.}
One runner boundary supplies the resolved root in both the child argument list
and child environment before any check or driver resolves a data path.  The
raw log records that executed value.  A self-test starts with shell root A and
board root B, launches an instrumented child, and proves that every file comes
from B.  Additional adversarial arms cover a child that rereads or mutates its
own environment and a check that attempts path resolution before injection;
neither may obtain a green report with mixed roots.

\paragraph{Current warning-leg gap.}
One head-activation check asks a subprocess to emit a teaching warning but
tests only that the warning text appeared.  It does not also require the
subprocess return status to be zero.  A program can print the expected warning,
crash immediately afterward, and still satisfy that isolated leg.

\paragraph{Required warning-leg closure.}
The verdict is the conjunction of successful return status and the expected
warning content.  The raw log records both facts.  A mutation fixture prints
the correct warning and then raises; it must make the leg and its owning gate
red rather than proving only that some text was produced before failure.

\subsection{Selection, tiers, dependencies, and resume}

The runner can select gate identifiers, a tier, or all gates at and after a
named entry.  Selection is validated against the registry before execution.
A misspelled \code{--gate}, \code{--from}, or \code{--force-rerun}
identifier produces a nonzero usage error with nearby-name suggestions.  The
board self-test drives these public arguments and proves that an empty or
dependency-skipped selection cannot report success.

A dependency states that one gate consumes an artifact or boundary produced
by another.  For example, adapter parity depends on successful save/rebuild.
A dependency is not merely earlier list order: the runner confirms its verdict
before the dependent body proceeds.

Resume skips a prior pass only when the currently implemented gate-code and
input digests still match.  It distinguishes stale code, stale inputs,
interruption, failure, and dependency skip; only current PASS is green.
Force-rerun invalidates selected records without deleting unrelated logs.

\begin{table*}[t]
\centering
\begin{tabular}{p{0.20\textwidth}p{0.32\textwidth}p{0.38\textwidth}}
\toprule
Stored situation & What it means & What the runner must do now \\
\midrule
Current \code{PASS} & Code, declared inputs, and raw-log digest still match &
Reuse the pass unless the operator explicitly forces a rerun. \\
Stale code & An executable member changed & Rerun; the old log remains
historical evidence for its old executable surface. \\
Stale input & A declared fixture or configuration input changed & Rerun with
the new input identity. \\
Pre-manifest & The gate now declares an executable manifest but its stored
PASS predates it & Rerun; the old record's narrower digest cannot certify
the declared surface. \\
Stale log & The raw log is absent, truncated, edited, or fails its digest &
Rerun; a database status cannot substitute for its evidence. \\
Interrupted & The body began but did not write a terminal gate verdict &
Rerun the interrupted gate.  Earlier independent current passes may remain
reusable. \\
Stored \code{FAIL} & The last complete execution was red & Rerun after a
bounded repair; never resume it as green. \\
Dependency skip & A prerequisite was not green & Run or repair the
prerequisite before the dependent gate. \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\caption{Resume states and their operational meaning.  ``Resume'' means
reusing evidence from an earlier invocation rather than executing the gate
body again.  A digest is a compact fingerprint of bytes; matching digests
support identity, while a mismatch proves that at least one byte changed.}
\label{tab:resume-states}
\end{table*}

\paragraph{Current gap.}
The manifest machinery is landed but no live gate declares one yet.  Until a
gate is populated, its stored digest covers only the gate function and the
check scripts named literally inside it, and a committed change in an
imported adapter or generator leaves that digest unchanged.  Population is
per gate, and a populated gate's earlier PASS reads as pre-manifest and
reruns, so the migration is deliberately incremental rather than a flag
day.

\paragraph{Required closure.}
One canonical executable-surface definition is shared by dirty preflight and
resume identity.  Most of it is current behavior now.  A declared gate's
membership is derived from its roots, persisted beside the digest as
per-file hashes, and revalidated on every invocation; a dynamic import
assembled from a string must sit in a reviewed waiver table naming the roots
that cover it; a subprocess target that no import graph shows must be a
declared root; a missing, truncated, or digest-mismatched raw log is
stale-log and reruns.  The remaining closure is population: each gate's
declared roots and named input keys, reviewed one gate at a time.

\begin{figure*}[t]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=0.90\textwidth]
  {texnotes/figures/fig11_gate_dependencies.pdf}
\caption{A common evidence dependency.  Identity establishes local
mathematics, smoke establishes the real provider path, save/rebuild
establishes persistence, and adapter/sampling gates establish external use.}
\label{fig:gate-deps}
\end{figure*}

\subsection{Capabilities and where a claim is allowed to run}

Each gate declares capabilities such as PyTorch, CosmoLike, Cobaya, and GPU.
The runner checks them before the body.  Capability declaration prevents a
missing dependency from being mistaken for a numerical failure, but it does
not turn every missing capability into a pass.

Pure validation and NumPy algebra run on CPU.  A claim about CUDA compilation
must run on CUDA.  A claim about Apple MPS float16 must run on Apple hardware.
When a capability is optional, the board uses a distinct non-green skip state
and states what remains unproven.  Catching every exception and exiting zero
would erase the difference between unsupported, broken, and correct.

Hardware controls remain useful.  A CPU or CUDA calculation that does not
overflow records why that backend is only a control, while the affected MPS
calculation supplies discrimination.  The contract follows executed dtype and
device, not a broad assumption that every accelerator behaves identically.

\subsection{Anatomy of a pure numeric check}

A pure check under \code{gates/checks} is an executable Python file with a
\code{main} function.  It imports the production function, creates a bounded
fixture, calculates an independent reference, and accumulates named
assertions.  If any assertion fails, the process raises or exits nonzero.

The reference does not call the production helper under test.  For a
covariance contraction, the production side may use a banded implementation
while the reference uses explicit loops and dense arithmetic on a tiny array.
For a geometry, the reference may form the physical residual and direct
inverse-covariance product.  Agreement is valuable because the algorithms do
not share the same possible mistake.

Fixtures are designed for discrimination rather than realism alone.  A
constant array can make correct and wrong axis orders coincide.  An affine
array can make several interpolation stencils exact.  A strong fixture assigns
distinct values to relevant coordinates and includes a control where the
correct path is known to agree.  The check prints actual and expected values
so a red log is diagnostic rather than merely boolean.

\subsection{Anatomy of a training smoke}

A smoke YAML is small but production-shaped.  It uses the real driver,
resolver, loaders, model, loss, optimizer, evaluation, and saving path.  Small
means fewer rows or epochs; it does not mean a second miniature trainer.

A collapse bar requires the network to learn more than a dead baseline.  For
an analytic scalar target, the baseline may always return the training mean.
The acceptance bar belongs below that baseline.  Merely requiring a finite
final loss allows an unchanged or disconnected network to pass.

Banners reveal resolved facts that are hard to infer from one metric:
activation, normalization, phase, learning rate, scheduler cadence, and source
artifact.  They are readbacks, not truth sources.  A behavioral leg accompanies
a banner whenever the configuration might be printed but ignored.

\subsection{Test doubles and monkeypatch scope}

A stub returns predetermined values.  A fake implements a small working
collaborator.  A monkeypatch temporarily replaces the object referenced by
production code.  Replacing CAMB with a fake can prove that an adapter
requests and combines keys correctly; it cannot prove CAMB returns the
assumed convention.

Patch scope must match the lookup site.  Replacing a class definition in one
module does not affect another module that already imported and bound the old
class.  A gate patches the name looked up by the production function and
restores it before later control arms.

A convention-honest fake makes confusable representations genuinely
different.  For CMB lensing it assigns different arrays to raw
\(C_L^{\phi\phi}\) and the scaled representation.  If the fake used equal
arrays, the wrong convention would pass.

\subsection{Mutation arms establish catch power}

A mutation arm deliberately reinstates one plausible defect.  The unchanged
gate must fail under the mutation and pass under the production path.
Examples include restoring width-squared chi-square tolerance, feeding scaled
lensing spectra where raw spectra are required, using the old non-Gaussian
weight, and rebuilding under a drifted default.

The mutation is targeted.  Changing many facts at once would not identify
which assertion carries the catch power.  Mutation evidence also detects a
self-referential test: if actual and expected call the same helper, changing
that helper changes both and the check remains green.

\subsection{Tolerance is a derived part of the claim}

Floating-point equality can be exact, absolute, relative, or combined.
Bitwise equality is appropriate when saving and loading the same tensor
should perform no arithmetic.  Relative tolerance is appropriate when the
expected magnitude varies.  Absolute tolerance supplies a floor near zero.

For a sum of \(w\) float32 terms, the chi-square domain band scales with
accumulation width \(w\) and machine epsilon.  It does not scale with
\(w^2\), which would admit materially negative scores.  The band is computed
from validated shape facts, not the possibly corrupt value being screened.

For example, float32 machine epsilon is approximately
\(\epsilon_{32}=1.1921\times10^{-7}\).  A kept residual width of $w=780$
gives the declared domain band
\begin{align*}
 b&=\max(10^{-6},32\epsilon_{32}w)\\
  &\simeq 2.98\times10^{-3}.
\end{align*}
A computed score of $-10^{-3}$ lies inside this roundoff allowance and is
normalized to the exact physical boundary zero.  A score of $-10^{-2}$
lies outside it and is rejected before ranking.  Replacing $w$ by $w^2$
would widen the same example to about $2.32$, allowing an impossible
negative score to look perfect.  The numbers show why ``some small negative
tolerance'' is not an adequate specification: dtype and contraction width are
part of the claim.

Every widened tolerance needs a measured valid control and a recorded
derivation.  A tolerance is not adjusted merely until a red result turns
green; that would let the defect define its own acceptance region.

\subsection{Raw logs and evidence readback}

Each raw log begins with gate identity, home documentation, Git commit, and
capabilities.  It records commands and complete output.  Named lines state the
value behind each check, and the final line is the gate verdict.

A compact illustrative excerpt is
\begin{verbatim}
gate: scalar-identity
commit: 1a2b3c4
leg scalar-identity.roundtrip: PASS
  max_abs=2.1e-07 tolerance=1.0e-06
leg scalar-identity.bad-name: PASS
  refusal=unknown scalar column
gate verdict: PASS (2 declared, 2 executed)
\end{verbatim}
The first leg's label, measured value, and tolerance explain a numerical pass.
The second leg proves a malformed name was refused; ``PASS'' refers to the
refusal behaving correctly.  The final counts establish completeness only
when the runner has reconciled the declared and executed identifiers.  This
excerpt teaches the intended record shape; it is not quoted workstation
evidence.

\code{logs/BOARD.md} is an index, not a replacement for evidence.  A reviewer
opens the raw log, confirms every advertised leg executed, and reads values
near thresholds.  A pass at 4.99 percent under a 5 percent bar carries
different operational risk from a pass at 0.1 percent.

Readback comes from the real consumer surface.  A value in an in-memory
configuration does not prove the saved HDF5 record contains it.  The gate
reopens the artifact or reads the adapter's public result to close that loop.

\subsection{Backlog tier: training and data contracts}

\subsubsection{\code{ema-off-identity}: the absent feature is a true no-op}

\textbf{Claim and path.}  Disabling the exponential moving average, EMA,
leaves pre-EMA training byte-identical.  The normal driver runs on the current
tree and in a temporary worktree at the pinned pre-EMA commit.  A worktree is
a second checkout sharing Git objects; it does not switch the user's active
checkout.

\textbf{Fixture and verdict.}  Both runs use the short gate YAML.  The scanner
extracts declared epoch lines and compares their bytes.  The current-tree run
also exercises a functional smoke so an empty comparison cannot pass.

\textbf{Catch power.}  Creating an averaged copy in the off branch, changing
selection, consuming randomness, or changing optimizer order alters a line.
This gate does not prove EMA-on behavior; the next gate owns that claim.

\subsubsection{\code{ema-smoke}: the averaged state participates in a run}

\textbf{Claim and path.}  With EMA enabled, the epoch-based horizon is used
and a plateau rewind restores coherent state.  A production training run uses
with \code{ema.horizon\_epochs=3}; the normal optimizer, scheduler, selection,
and rewind code execute.

\textbf{Fixture and verdict.}  The YAML causes a learning-rate cut during the
short run.  Banners must identify the horizon and rewind, and the process must
finish with the expected metrics.

\textbf{Catch power.}  Removing the EMA update, converting the horizon
incorrectly, or rewinding live weights without their averaged partner removes
a required observation.

\subsubsection{\code{production-diagnostic}: one report crosses several boundaries}

\textbf{Claim and path.}  The production diagnostic command can stage cut
data, train, and create the expected report while exposing accurate size and
coverage facts.  The cosmic-shear driver runs with \code{--diagnostic} and
uses production plotting code.

\textbf{Fixture and verdict.}  The gate checks the model-class census, rows
surviving the density window, printed train/validation sizes, and shaded
coverage triangle.  A file suffix alone is not acceptance.

\textbf{Catch power.}  Dead model branches, cuts applied after selection,
misreported sizes, or a plot omitting the declared window breaks a leg.

\subsubsection{\code{single-phase-demotion}: phase keys are handled deliberately}

\textbf{Claim and path.}  A single-phase \code{resmlp} can receive the
documented phase-shaped configuration without a traceback, while a structured
model retains two-phase behavior.  Both pass through the real resolver and
driver.

\textbf{Fixture and verdict.}  The single-phase fixture contains head-shaped
keys and must train under the declared demotion.  A two-phase control must
still execute separate phases.

\textbf{Catch power.}  Forwarding a head-only option into \code{resmlp}
reproduces the old failure.  Globally deleting phase settings makes the
two-phase control fail.

\subsubsection{\code{head-scheduler-override}: the head owns its cadence}

\textbf{Claim and path.}  A head scheduler replaces the relevant top-level
settings and cuts the head learning rate on its own patience.  The real
two-phase resolver constructs the scheduler and the epoch loop feeds its
validation metric.

\textbf{Fixture and verdict.}  The override uses patience ten.  The resolved
banner must name it and the cut must occur on the matching cadence.

\textbf{Catch power.}  A shallow merge that retains top-level patience, a
scheduler attached to the wrong optimizer, or a metric-free step shifts or
removes the cut.

\subsubsection{\code{eval-batch-invariance}: partitioning is not mathematics}

\textbf{Claim and path.}  Validation scores do not depend on how the same
ordered rows are partitioned.  The check calls real \code{eval\_val} with
several batch sizes, including its production final-batch padding path.

\textbf{Fixture and verdict.}  Per-row scores and aggregate metrics agree at
relative tolerance \(10^{-6}\).  Timing is reported but is not a numerical
verdict.

\textbf{Catch power.}  Counting padded duplicates, leaking state between
batches, batch-relative normalization, or dropping a final short batch
changes at least one per-row score.

\subsubsection{\code{finite-contract}: impossible scores never rank}

\textbf{Claim and path.}  NaN, infinity, and materially negative chi-square
values are rejected at training, validation, diagnostics, and warm-start
parity boundaries.  The PyTorch check calls the production reduction,
\code{eval\_val}, source diagnostic, safe square roots, and parity helpers.

\textbf{Fixture and verdict.}  Red fixtures include NaN in either parity arm,
a nonfinite transfer surface, exact-fit zero, finite losses near the float32
maximum, and finite negative chi-square.  Valid controls include analytic
positive square roots and tiny roundoff from an ill-conditioned
positive-definite contraction.  The allowed roundoff band scales with kept
per-row width, not width squared.

\textbf{Catch power.}  A mutation restoring the old width-squared band crowns
a materially negative production-width score as perfect.  Finite-only
validation lets NaN comparisons evade threshold counts.  On a supported
compile lane, an exception is failure rather than a green skip.

\subsubsection{\code{board-selftest}: the runner reports what actually ran}

\textbf{Claim and path.}  The board's own selection, dependency, resume,
atomic-status, and evidence-map machinery cannot manufacture a green command
from an empty, skipped, stale, or interrupted run.  The pure-Python check
drives the real \code{run\_board.main}, \code{select\_gates}, and resume
helpers with small fake Gate objects.

\textbf{Fixture and verdict.}  Fake gates pass, fail, skip through a failed
dependency, or raise an uncaught interruption.  Unknown selectors and force
targets must return nonzero with a suggestion.  Mutating a gate body,
referenced YAML, input config, evidence anchor, or cited log must invalidate
the corresponding record.  For the currently migrated structured-evidence
entries, every declared anchor must resolve to a real note location and every
identifier must be globally unique.  The board has forty registered gates,
but that count must not be confused with rollout completeness: most gates do
not yet declare every individual leg in the structured evidence map.

\textbf{Catch power.}  A status-only resume rule, warning-only selector, log
overwrite, or board row whose note anchor does not exist makes one of the
fake scenarios falsely green and is rejected.  This gate tests harness
control flow; it does not prove any scientific gate body.

\subsubsection{\code{generator-seed}: sampling owns one recorded random stream}

\textbf{Claim and path.}  Generator sampling is reproducible from one required
integer seed.  The seed constructs an owned NumPy \code{Generator} that is
threaded through uniform draws, walker initialization, sampler moves, and
thinning rather than reading process-global \code{np.random} state.

\textbf{Fixture and verdict.}  Two runs with the same seed produce identical
draws and the chain header records that seed.  Invalid seed types fail before
sampling.  A monkeypatch of global random functions must not affect the owned
stream.

\textbf{Catch power.}  One leftover global draw changes the same-seed result
or triggers the monkeypatch.  The pure gate proves ownership and local
reproducibility; append/restart replay and MPI worker-count invariance require
their generator smoke legs.

\subsubsection{\code{cli-strict}: misspelled flags stop before expensive work}

\textbf{Claim and path.}  Every public executable uses strict argument
parsing.  The check performs a source census and drives representative driver
\code{main} functions through their real parsers while replacing the
expensive training boundary with an instrumented stub.

\textbf{Fixture and verdict.}  A valid command reaches the stub exactly once.
The misspelling \code{--activaton} exits nonzero, names the unrecognized
argument, and reaches the stub zero times.  All public entry points must use
\code{parse\_args}, not \code{parse\_known\_args}.

\textbf{Catch power.}  Silently retaining unknown arguments or manually
discarding parser leftovers lets the misspelled option train a default model;
the zero-call assertion exposes that behavior.

\subsubsection{\code{family-first}: each driver owns one data family}

\textbf{Claim and path.}  A direct driver selects one physical data-block
family before experiment construction.  The cosmic-shear driver cannot
become a CMB, scalar, background, or matter-power run merely because the YAML
contains that block, while each thin family wrapper accepts its own block.

\textbf{Fixture and verdict.}  Wrong-family configurations fail at startup
with both expected and received families.  A clean cosmic-shear configuration
reaches training, and the four family wrappers reach their matching boundary.
A census verifies that every cosmic-shear campaign pins the same family.

\textbf{Catch power.}  Restoring automatic family dispatch makes a
wrong-driver fixture run.  Pinning only the single-run driver leaves a sweep
or search census failure, which is why the gate covers the driver family, not
one filename.

\subsubsection{\code{stage-ram}: the memory decision counts every copy}

\textbf{Claim and path.}  \code{stage\_source} budgets the compact parameter
copy, compact target copy, and row-reindex storage before choosing resident or
file-backed staging.  Parameter and target widths and dtypes are counted
separately.

\textbf{Fixture and verdict.}  A narrow target with a wide parameter table is
chosen so target bytes alone fit but the coordinated copies exceed the
budget.  The real stage function must stay disk-backed.  Resident and
disk-backed controls return byte-identical selected rows, including an
unequal-dtype case.

\textbf{Catch power.}  A mutation restoring the old target-only estimate
selects resident storage and fails the regime verdict even though its returned
numbers remain correct.  This separates resource truth from numerical truth.

\subsubsection{\code{artifact-readback}: stored values keep their types}

\textbf{Claim and path.}  Artifact Boolean attributes are parsed by an
explicit typed reader, not Python truthiness.  The check exercises the shared
reader and scans every artifact Boolean read site.

\textbf{Fixture and verdict.}  A native Boolean is accepted, an absent key
uses its named default, and string or integer lookalikes---including the
truthy string \code{"False"}---raise with file and schema context.  The
census requires all read sites to use the shared boundary.

\textbf{Catch power.}  Replacing the reader with \code{bool(value)} turns
\code{"False"} into true and can select drifted transfer weights.  This
pure gate proves type parsing and source coverage; the live save/forge/rebuild
artifact leg remains a separate workstation obligation.

\subsubsection{\code{diagnostics-domain}: invalid scores do not become reports}

\textbf{Claim and path.}  Diagnostic producers apply the same finite,
nonnegative chi-square boundary as training and evaluation before converting
scores into coverage fractions or residual summaries.  The check calls the
real local-linear floor and CMB residual diagnostic and censes grid-family
producer sites.

\textbf{Fixture and verdict.}  Valid scores pass byte-identically; negative
roundoff inside the width-derived band becomes exact zero; materially negative,
NaN, and infinite values raise with boundary, rows, and band.  A reachable
one-coordinate negative floor is refused before \code{f\_floor} is formed.

\textbf{Catch power.}  Bypassing the screen recreates the former false
\code{f\_floor=0} ``perfect'' result.  A valid diagnostic control prevents the
repair from converting all small or difficult results into errors.

\subsubsection{\code{berhu-loss}: the objective matches its piecewise law}

\textbf{Claim and path.}  The reverse-Huber objective has its declared value
and derivative, and a head can select it independently of a square-root
trunk.  A pure check calls the production reduction and autograd; a short
two-phase run exercises schema resolution.

\textbf{Fixture and verdict.}  Analytic points lie below, on, and above the
knot and cap.  Required continuity is checked, while banners name square root
for the trunk and capped BerHu for the head.

\textbf{Catch power.}  Using residual-norm rather than chi-square units,
swapping a branch inequality, or resolving the head to the trunk loss changes
an analytic value or banner.

\subsubsection{\code{loss-schema-equivalence}: syntax migration preserves meaning}

\textbf{Claim and path.}  Moving loss settings into the nested schema does not
change an equivalent old run.  The ordinary driver resolves and trains both
forms.

\textbf{Fixture and verdict.}  Selected numerical epoch lines reproduce the
pre-migration result.

\textbf{Catch power.}  Reading a key from the wrong nesting level, falling
back to a new default, or accepting conflicting spellings changes those
lines.  This equivalence check complements, but does not replace, the analytic
loss gate.

\subsubsection{\code{berhu-anneal}: endpoints have mathematical meaning}

\textbf{Claim and path.}  BerHu annealing begins as square root, stays
continuous at the hold boundary, and reaches full BerHu at the declared
endpoint.  The shared production schedule supplies the blend coefficient.

\textbf{Fixture and verdict.}  Values immediately around the hold boundary
are compared, the epoch-15 fixture must have coefficient one, and a no-anneal
control preserves absent-key behavior.

\textbf{Catch power.}  Reversing an increasing schedule, an off-by-one
boundary, or treating \code{const} as a generated ramp changes a sampled
coefficient.

\subsubsection{\code{ema-anneal}: the average becomes live at the intended time}

\textbf{Claim and path.}  EMA annealing excludes the deliberately poor early
trajectory and evaluates averaged weights at the live point.  The normal EMA
update, shared schedule, and model-selection path execute.

\textbf{Fixture and verdict.}  A no-anneal control is compared with an
annealed run; output identifies the hold and metrics from the live averaged
state.

\textbf{Catch power.}  Updating during the hold, interpreting the horizon in
the wrong unit, or evaluating raw weights under an EMA banner breaks the
transition.

\subsubsection{\code{param-window-cuts}: selection follows physical cuts}

\textbf{Claim and path.}  A tight density window uses named parameter columns,
shrinks the candidate pool by the independent count, and then trains.  The
